A necessary condition for a candidate to match: it must be possible to set parameters so that (i) all extra non-GT functional forms vanish (e.g., \(A^{-2}\), \(A^{-1/3}\), \(\exp(\text{const}\cdot|A|)\), constants), (ii) the remaining \(t\)-dependence is exactly \(-0.1013\,A e^{-0.07564 t}\), and (iii) the remaining \(A\)-dependence matches the rational \(A^2/(1+\alpha A^4)\) plus a linear \(-0.1013A\).

Below, each candidate fails one or more of these necessary conditions.

GT Equivalence Verification (CRK29)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A - c1*A*exp(-c2*_s*t) + c3*_z*A**c4/(c5*A**c6 + c7)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.82602416619319257*A**2/(0.8635828411814722*A**4 + 1) - 0.10132643987768028*A - 0.10132643987768028*A*exp(-0.075641032147212359*t)`

The GT has three terms:
1. A rational term: `c*A²/(d*A⁴ + 1)` 
2. A linear term: `-c₀*A`
3. An exponential-decay term: `-c₁*A*exp(-k*t)`

Key structural features of GT:
- Linear in A (coefficient of A)
- A*exp(αt) term (time-dependent)
- A²/(A⁴ + const) rational term
- No exp(A) terms, no A⁻², no A⁻¹/³, no A³ terms, no |A| vs A issues (A≥0 domain)

Under the domain constraint A ≥ 0, |A| = A and Max(0,A) = A.

For a candidate to match GT, all extra basis functions must be eliminable (set coefficients to 0), and the remaining structure must be algebraically equivalent to GT.

**Critical observation:** The GT rational term is `A²/(c*A⁴+1)`. Many candidates have terms like `A⁴/(c+A⁴)` or `1/(c+A⁴)`. Let me check:
- `A⁴/(c₇+A⁴)` cannot equal `A²/(c*A⁴+1)` — different rational function structure
- `1/(c₇+A⁴)` — can we combine with other terms to get `A²/(c*A⁴+1)`? Only if there's an A² multiplier somewhere.

Note: `A²/(c*A⁴+1)` can be rewritten but NOT as `A⁴/(A⁴+c)` or `1/(A⁴+c)` — these are fundamentally different rational functions.

Most candidates (1-27, 32-38, 49-50) contain terms like `exp(c*|A|)`, `A⁻²`, `A⁻¹/³`, `A³`, `A⁴/(c+A⁴)`, or `1/(c+A⁴)`. Setting exp(c*|A|) coefficients to 0 removes that term, and setting A⁻², A⁻¹/³ coefficients to 0 removes those. But the rational term structure must match.

Let me check candidates with `A²/(c+A⁴)`-type or flexible exponent structures:

**Candidates 28, 29, 30, 31, 34, 40, 42, 45, 46, 48:** These have flexible exponents (c6, c7, c8, etc.) that could potentially create `A²/(A⁴+c)`.

**Candidate 29:** `c0*exp(c1*|A|) + c2 + c3*exp(c4*t)*|A| + c5*|A|^c6/(c7+|A|^c6) + c8/A²`
Set c0=0, c2=0, c8=0. Remaining: `c3*exp(c4*t)*A + c5*A^c6/(c7+A^c6)`. But `A^c6/(c7+A^c6)` ≠ `A²/(c*A⁴+1)`. If c6=2: `A²/(c7+A²)` ≠ `A²/(c*A⁴+1)`. If c6=4: `A⁴/(c7+A⁴)` ≠ `A²/(c*A⁴+1)`. Missing the linear -c₀*A term too. No match.

**Candidate 40:** `c0 + c1*exp(c2*t)*|A| + c3*A² + c4*A + (c5+A^c6)^c7 * A^c6`
Set c0=0, c3=0. Need `(c5+A^c6)^c7 * A^c6` to equal `A²/(c*A⁴+1)`. If c6=4, c7=-1: `A⁴/(c5+A⁴)` ≠ `A²/(A⁴+c)`. If c6=2, c7=-1: `A²/(c5+A²)` — no. Cannot match.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can produce the exact rational structure `A²/(c*A⁴+1)` from their available terms. The candidates either have `A⁴/(c+A⁴)`, `1/(c+A⁴)`, `A^n/(c+A^n)` (same exponent), or power-law combinations that cannot replicate this.
